            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon-based nanocomposites have been extensively studied in energy storage and conversion systems because of their superior electrochem. performance.  However, the majority of metal oxides are grown on the surface of carbonaceous material.  Herein, a different strategy is reported of constructing V2O5 within the metal org. framework derived carbonaceous dodecahedrons.  Vanadium precursor is absorbed into the porous dodecahedron-shaped carbon framework first and then in situ converted into V2O5 within the carbonaceous framework in the annealing process in air.  As cathode materials for lithium ion batteries, the porous V2O5@C composites exhibit enhanced electrochem. performance, due to the synergistic effect of V2O5 and carbon composite.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqSeWdds_QgNLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-J66Vta9yow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XpsFGqsL0%253D&amp;md5=866734c8e67c4c4144597b84c037ad16</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201500196"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">FeSe<sub>2</sub> Microspheres as a High-Performance Anode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">FeSe2 Microspheres as a High-Performance Anode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Hu, Zhe; Liu, Xue; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The use is demonstrated of FeSe2 as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  The FeSe2 microspheres assembled by nanooctahedra display a high tapping d. of 1.85 g cm-3 and a discharge capacity of 447 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1.  The FeSe2 anode also exhibits long-term cyclic stability (372 mA h g-1 with capacity retention of 89.0% after 2000 cycles at 1 A g-1 ) and excellent high-rate performance 388 mA h g-1 at 10 C, 337 mA h g-1 at 20 C, 226 mA h g-1 at 50 C, where 1 C = 0.5 A g-1.  The conversion reaction of FeSe2 + 4Na+ + 4e ↔ Fe + 2Na2Se has been confirmed.  Furthermore, the FeSe2 anode is coupled with an excessive Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode (the capacity of the Na3V2(PO4)3 is 1.5-2 times more than that of FeSe2) to fabricate a full cell, which exhibits a discharge capacity of 366 mA h g-1 based on the mass of FeSe2 with an av. output voltage of about 1.7 V at 1 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqNZQmIWuA02rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-J66Vta9yow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmslens7Y%253D&amp;md5=0ecc7e52e3b809d3dadbf828186e0859</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-017-1847-1"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced Sodium Storage Performance in Flexible Free-Standing Multichannel Carbon Nanofibers with Enlarged Interlayer Spacing</span>. <i>Nano Res.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2256</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2264</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced sodium storage performance in flexible free-standing multichannel carbon nanofibers with enlarged interlayer spacing</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Beibei; Zeng, Linchao; Sun, Xizhen; Yu, Yan; Wang, Qingsong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A flexible and free-standing multichannel carbon nanofiber (MCNF) film electrode was fabricated through electrospinning and carbonization.  After high-temp. treatment of MCNFs in vacuum, the obtained fibers (MCNFs-V) had a dilated interlayer spacing of graphene sheets (0.398 nm) and an ultra-low sp. surface area (15.3 m2/g).  When used as an anode for sodium-ion batteries, the MCNFs-V showed a discharge plateau below 0.1 V, and sodium was intercalated into the stacked graphene sheets layers during the sodiation process.  The MCNFs-V exhibited a reversible and high specific capacity of 222 mAh/g at a c.d. of 0.1 A/g after 100 cycles and excellent long-term cycling stability, which was superior to that of MCNFs.  The improved sodium storage performance was attributed to the unique microstructure of the MCNFs-V with an enlarged interlayer spacing of graphene sheets for sodium intercalation.  The MCNFs-V electrode holds great promise as an anode material for com. sodium-ion batteries.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured binary and ternary metal sulfides: synthesis methods and their application in energy conversion and storage devices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kulkarni, Pranav; Nataraj, S. K.; Balakrishna, R. Geetha; Nagaraju, D. H.; Reddy, M. V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">22040-22094</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal sulfides, known as being analogous to metal oxides, have emerged as a new class of materials for energy conversion and/or storage applications due to their low cost and high electrochem. activity.  They have shown fascinating properties such as excellent redox reversibility, cond., and capacitance.  Further, binary metal sulfides have gained enormous attention due to their large redox reaction sites and high elec. cond. compared to metal sulfides.  Recently, use of binary metal sulfides as electrode materials for various applications such as lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), supercapacitors (SC), and solar cells has been extensively studied by various research groups and this review critically overviews the strategies and advances made towards attaining high performances from these sulfides in an effort to provide leads for scale-up and to find long term solns. for energy and environment crisis.  Finally, challenges in achieving superior performances and the future scope of research for metal sulfide based energy materials have been outlined.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpTek6t2S6vj7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-J66Vta9yow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsVyitbjE&amp;md5=a0a162b6fecd5b94e06c71109ea21bd9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201200691"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Slater, M.

                        cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Slater, Michael D.; Kim, Donghan; Lee, Eungje; Doeff, Marca; Johnson, Christopher S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.  The engineering modeling calcns. of Na-ion battery energy d. indicate that 210 Wh kg-1 in gravimetric energy is possible for Na-ion batteries compared to existing Li-ion technol. if a cathode capacity of 200 mAh g-1 and a 500 mAh g-1 anode can be discovered with an av. cell potential of 3.3 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojsFXLPEQzILVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-J66Vta9yow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XntlSnurc%253D&amp;md5=fa5d7d089d261a40896cb6b03e88bfbe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1039/C4CC01033G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rahman, M.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrasmall Sn Nanoparticles Embedded in Carbon as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Jiao, Lifang; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designed as a high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life anode for Na-ion batteries, ultra-small Sn nanoparticles (≈8 nm) homogeneously embedded in spherical C network (denoted as 8-Sn@C) is prepd. using an aerosol spray pyrolysis method.  Instrumental analyses show that 8-Sn@C nanocomposite with 46% Sn and a BET surface area of 150.43 m2 g-1 delivers an initial reversible capacity of ≈493.6 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 200 mA g-1, a high-rate capacity of 349 mA h g-1 even at 4000 mA g-1, and a stable capacity of ≈415 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1000 mA g-1.  The remarkable electrochem. performance of 8-Sn@C is owing to the synergetic effects between the well-dispersed ultra-small Sn nanoparticles and the conductive C network.  This unique structure of very-fine Sn nanoparticles embedded in the porous C network can effectively suppress the vol. fluctuation and particle aggregation of Sn during prolonged sodiation/desodiation process, thus solving the major problems of pulverization, loss of elec. contact and low use rate facing Sn anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIJZ-8q45agLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKxY-hpupPDA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Preparation of nitrogen- and phosphorus co-doped carbon microspheres and their superior performance as anode in sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yueming; Wang, Zhiguang; Li, Linlin; Peng, Shengjie; Zhang, Long; Srinivasan, Madhavi; Ramakrishna, Seeram</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">99</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are considered a top alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale renewable energy storage units due to their low cost and the abundance of sodium-bearing precursors in the earth's mineral deposits.  However, the absence of a suitable neg. electrode material hinders their development.  In this contribution, we report the prepn. of nitrogen and phosphorous co-doped carbon microspheres through a hydrothermal process followed by heat treatment in presence of (NH4)2HPO4 and investigate their electrochem. performance as anode in sodium-ion batteries.  Benefiting from the N, P co-doping, the obtained N, P co-doped carbon microspheres demonstrates high specific capacity, excellent cycle stability as well as good rate performance.  The as prepd. N, P co-doped carbon microspheres can deliver a reversible capacity of 305 mAh/g at a c.d. of 0.1 A/g and even deliver a capacity of 136 mAh/g at 5 A/g.  This superior sodium storage performance of N, P co-doped carbon makes it as a promising low-cost anode candidate for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpIqaRi021LVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKxY-hpupPDA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitance-boosted ultrafast Na storage in a pie-like FeS@C nanohybrid as an advanced anode material for sodium-ion full batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Bao-Hua; Wang, Ying-Ying; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Ning, Qiu-Li; Xi, Xiao-Tong; Pang, Wei-Lin; Cao, An-Min; Wang, Xinlong; Zhang, Jing-Ping; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9218-9225</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In order to develop promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), a novel pie-like FeS@C (P-FeS@C) nanohybrid, in which all ultrasmall FeS nanocrystals (NCs) are completely embedded into the carbon network and sealed by a protective carbon shell, has been prepd.  The unique pie-like structure can effectively speed up the kinetics of electrode reactions, while the carbon shell stabilizes the FeS NCs inside.  Studies show that the electrochem. reaction processes of P-FeS@C electrodes are dominated by the pseudocapacitive behavior, leading to an ultrafast Na+-insertion/extn. reaction.  Hence, the prepd. P-FeS@C nanohybrid exhibits superior Na-storage properties esp. high rate capability in half cells.  For example, it can deliver reversible capacities of 555.1 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 over 150 cycles and about 60.4 mA h g-1 at 80 A g-1 (an ultrahigh c.d. even higher than that of the capacitor test).  Furthermore, an advanced P-FeS@C//Na3V2(PO4)2O2F full cell has been assembled out, which delivers a stable specific capacity of 441.2 mA h g-1 after 80 cycles at 0.5 A g-1 with a capacity retention of 91.8%.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGonBrKimr3tJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKxY-hpupPDA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXnsVegsLc%253D&amp;md5=5abf0036cac7063327820faad7081671</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201703086"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">1D Nanomaterials: Design, Synthesis, and Applications in Sodium–Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1703086</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1039/C4NR03057E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rui, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanostructured Metal Sulfides for Energy Storage</span>. <i>Nanoscale</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">9889</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">9924</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C4NR03057E</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D9889-9924%26journal%3DNanoscale%26author%3DX.%2BRui%26author%3DH.%2BTan%26author%3DQ.%2BYan%26title%3DNanostructured%2BMetal%2BSulfides%2Bfor%2BEnergy%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC4NR03057E&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11984&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC4NR03057E&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured metal sulfides for energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rui, Xianhong; Tan, Huiteng; Yan, Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9889-9924</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Advanced electrodes with a high energy d. at high power are urgently needed for high-performance energy storage devices, including lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and supercapacitors (SCs), to fulfill the requirements of future electrochem. power sources for applications such as in hybrid elec./plug-in-hybrid (HEV/PHEV) vehicles.  Metal sulfides with unique phys. and chem. properties, as well as high specific capacity/capacitance, which are typically multiple times higher than that of the carbon/graphite-based materials, are currently studied as promising electrode materials.  However, the implementation of these sulfide electrodes in practical applications is hindered by their inferior rate performance and cycling stability.  Nanostructures offering the advantages of high surface-to-vol. ratios, favorable transport properties, and high freedom for the vol. change upon ion insertion/extn. and other reactions, present an opportunity to build next-generation LIBs and SCs.  Thus, the development of novel concepts in material research to achieve new nanostructures paves the way for improved electrochem. performance.  Herein, we summarize recent advances in nanostructured metal sulfides, such as iron sulfides, copper sulfides, cobalt sulfides, nickel sulfides, manganese sulfides, molybdenum sulfides, tin sulfides, with zero-, one-, two-, and three-dimensional morphologies for LIB and SC applications.  In addn., the recently emerged concept of incorporating conductive matrixes, esp. graphene, with metal sulfide nanomaterials will also be highlighted.  Finally, some remarks are made on the challenges and perspectives for the future development of metal sulfide-based LIB and SC devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGobIED_9cAgE7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgNz3FmI3sCmg"> &gt;&gt; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ramakrishna, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unique Cobalt Sulfide/Reduced Graphene Oxide Composite as an Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Superior Rate Capability and Long Cycling Stability</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1359</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smll.201502788</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D1359%26journal%3DSmall%26author%3DS.%2BPeng%26author%3DX.%2BHan%26author%3DL.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BZhu%26author%3DF.%2BCheng%26author%3DM.%2BSrinivansan%26author%3DS.%2BAdams%26author%3DS.%2BRamakrishna%26title%3DUnique%2BCobalt%2BSulfide%252FReduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%2BComposite%2Bas%2Ban%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2Bwith%2BSuperior%2BRate%2BCapability%2Band%2BLong%2BCycling%2BStability%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fsmll.201502788&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11984&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fsmll.201502788&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unique Cobalt Sulfide/Reduced Graphene Oxide Composite as an Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Superior Rate Capability and Long Cycling Stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Peng, Shengjie; Han, Xiaopeng; Li, Linlin; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Cheng, Fangyi; Srinivansan, Madhavi; Adams, Stefan; Ramakrishna, Seeram</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1359-1368</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploitation of high-performance anode materials is essential but challenging to the development of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Among all proposed anode materials for SIBs, sulfides were proved promising candidates due to their unique chem. and phys. properties.  A facile solvothermal method to in situ decorate cobalt sulfide (CoS) nanoplates on reduced graphene oxide (rGO) to build CoS@rGO composite is described.  When evaluated as anode for SIBs, an impressive high specific capacity (540 mAh/g at 1 A/g), excellent rate capability (636 mAh/g at 0.1 A/g and 306 mAh/g at 10 A/g), and extraordinarily cycle stability (420 mAh/g at 1 A/g after 1000 cycles) were demonstrated by CoS@rGO composite for sodium storage.  The synergetic effect between the CoS nanoplates and rGO matrix contributes to the enhanced electrochem. performance of the hybrid composite.  The results provide a facile approach to fabricate promising anode materials for high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGotD1r43G7-ibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgNz3FmI3sCmg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xns1Cjtw%253D%253D&amp;md5=7834a86a1d3c3333ee7594239160e829</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201502161"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Makaryan, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Van Aken, K.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured transition metal sulfides for lithium ion batteries: Progress and challenges</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xiaodong; Liu, Wen; Kim, Youngsik; Cho, Jaephil</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Today</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">604-630</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High performance lithium batteries are in great demand for consumer electronics, elec. vehicles and grid scale stationary energy storage.  Transition metal sulfides based on conversion or alloying reactions have drawn much attention because of their significantly higher specific capacity than traditional insertion electrode materials.  However, their poor cyclability caused by the large vol. change during the lithium (Li) up-taking and extn. has hindered their further developments and applications in Li rechargeable batteries.  This review outlines the fundamental mechanisms and obstacles of the transition metal sulfides assocd. with Li storage through conversion reaction and also discusses how the nanostructure design can successfully address their challenges.  Recent progresses in the nanoparticle synthesis, nanostructure design, composite fabrication, and their effects on the electrochem. performances are summarized and discussed.  In addn., remaining challenges and possibilities for further improvements are also prospected.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp2JhMA2FxxubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgNz3FmI3sCmg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhsFyrurjJ&amp;md5=127b26adc84cbc94edaf74b3949c6f8f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201602608"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, G.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Urchin-Like CoSe2 as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Park, Mihui; Zhou, Limin; Lee, Gi-Hyeok; Li, Weijie; Kang, Yong-Mook; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6728-6735</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Urchin-like CoSe2 assembled by nanorods was synthesized via simple solvothermal route and was 1st applied as an anode material for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) with ether-based electrolytes.  The CoSe2 delivers excellent sodiation and de-sodiation properties when using 1 M NaCF3SO3 in diethyleneglycol dimethylether as an electrolyte and cycling between 0.5 and 3.0 V.  A high discharge capacity of 0.410 A h g-1 is obtained at 1 A g-1 after 1800 cycles, corresponding to a capacity retention of 98.6% calcd. from the 30th cycle.  Even at an ultrahigh rate of 50 A g-1, the capacity still maintains 0.097 A h g-1.  The reaction mechanism of the as-prepd. CoSe2 is also studied.  At discharged 1.56 V, insertion reaction occurs, while 2 conversion reactions take place at the 2nd and 3rd plateaus around 0.98 and 0.65 V.  During the charge process, Co 1st reacts with Na2Se to form NaxCoSe2 and then turns back to CoSe2.  In addn. to Na/CoSe2 half cells, Na3V2(PO4)3/CoSe2 full cell with excessive amt. of Na3V2(PO4)3 was studied.  The full cell exhibits a reversible capacity of 0.380 Ah g-1.  This work enriches the possibilities for anode materials for SIBs with high performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpzIV0Nvfw2qrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgNz3FmI3sCmg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1GhtLnM&amp;md5=5a3155a0784f8e8bcf04652fe8bd5e08</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-016-1394-1"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Embedding CoS2 nanoparticles in N-doped carbon nanotube hollow frameworks for enhanced lithium storage properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jintao; Yu, Le; Lou, Xiong Wen David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4298-4304</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NRAEB5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1998-0000</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The construction of metal sulfides-carbon nanocomposites with a hollow structure is highly attractive for various energy storage and conversion technologies.  Herein, we report a facile two-step method for prepg. a nanocomposite with CoS2 nanoparticles in N-doped carbon nanotube hollow frameworks (NCNTFs).  Starting from zeolitic imidazolate framework-67 (ZIF-67) particles, in situ reduced metallic cobalt nanocrystals expedite the formation of the hierarchical hollow frameworks from staggered carbon nanotubes via a carbonization process.  After a follow-up sulfidation reaction with sulfur powder, the embedded cobalt crystals are transformed into CoS2 nanoparticles.  Benefitting from the robust hollow frameworks made of N-doped carbon nanotubes and highly active CoS2 ultrafine nanoparticles, this advanced nanocomposite shows greatly enhanced lithium storage properties when evaluated as an electrode for lithium-ion batteries.  Impressively, the resultant CoS2/NCNTF material delivers a high specific capacity of ∼937 mAh·g-1 at a c.d. of 1.0 A·g-1 with a cycle life longer than 160 cycles.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Different distribution of in-situ thin carbon layer in hollow cobalt sulfide nanocages and their application for supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin, Meng; Lu, Shi-Yu; Ma, Li; Gan, Meng-Yu; Lei, Yao; Zhang, Xiu-Ling; Fu, Gang; Yang, Pei-Shu; Yan, Mao-Fa</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

Thin carbon layer (TCL) coated has been regarded as a promising constructing strategy for high performance supercapacitors, because TCL can promote the tremendous properties of bare materials.  In this literature, we report a very interesting phenomenon that different distribution of in-situ carbon coated hollow CoS2 nanocages (external and both external and interior) can be synthesized only by adjusting sulfuration time, followed by calcination.  Moreover, it is clearly obsd. that CoS2-C@TCL exhibits significant improvement for specific capacitance and good stability (better than CoS2@TCL and CoS2).                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt Sulfide Quantum Dot Embedded N/S-Doped Carbon Nanosheets with Superior Reversibility and Rate Capability for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Qiubo; Ma, Yifan; Chen, Tingting; Xia, Qiuying; Yang, Mei; Xia, Hui; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12658-12667</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal sulfides are promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries due to their large specific capacities.  The practical applications of metal sulfides in sodium-ion batteries, however, are still limited due to their large vol. expansion, poor cycling stability, and sluggish electrode kinetics.  In this work, a two-dimensional heterostructure of CoSx (CoS and Co9S8) quantum dots embedded N/S-doped carbon nanosheets (CoSx@NSC) is prepd. by a sol-gel method.  The CoSx quantum dots are in situ formed within ultrafine carbon nanosheets without further sulfidation, thus resulting in ultrafine CoSx particle size and embedded heterostructure.  Meanwhile, enriched N and S codoping in the carbon nanosheets greatly enhances the elec. cond. for the conductive matrix and creates more active sites for sodium storage.  As a result, the hybrid CoSx@NSC electrode shows excellent rate capability (600 mAh g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 and 500 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1) and outstanding cycling stability (87% capacity retention after 200 cycles at 1 A g-1), making it promising as an anode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries.  A CoSx@NSC//Na0.44MnO2 full cell is demonstrated, and it can deliver a specific capacity of 414 mAh g-1 (based on the mass of CoSx@NSC) at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq9OkEmDbmxnrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg1OB31eJLUBA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvVaku7bJ&amp;md5=366aa605bfae1bf5095b737a7b5b3c40</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2017.12.014"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ali, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Asif, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cobalt Selenide Decorated Carbon Spheres for Excellent Cycling Performance of Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">19</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">28</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improved electrochemical performance of CoS2-MWCNT nanocomposites for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shadike, Zulipiya; Cao, Ming-Hui; Ding, Fei; Sang, Lin; Fu, Zheng-Wen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Communications (Cambridge, United Kingdom)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A CoS2/multi-walled carbon nanotube (MWCNT) nanocomposite was synthesized and its Na storage performances in ether-based electrolyte and commonly used carbonate-based electrolyte were studied for the 1st time.                 10.1039/C6RA12563H</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D70632-70637%26journal%3DRSC%2BAdv.%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26author%3DW.%2BFeng%26author%3DY.%2BLin%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DH.%2BFei%26title%3DFlaky%2BCoS2%2Band%2BGraphene%2BNanocomposite%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2Bwith%2BImproved%2BPerformance%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC6RA12563H&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11984&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC6RA12563H&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flaky CoS2 and graphene nanocomposite anode materials for sodium-ion batteries with improved performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhiwei; Feng, Wenjing; Lin, Yaqin; Liu, Xin; Fei, Hailong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">74</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">70632-70637</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A flaky CoS2 based reduced graphene oxide (CoS2/rGO) composite was successfully synthesized via a solvothermal route.  CoS2 nanoparticles with sizes of 20-30 nm are uniformly anchored on the reduced graphene oxide (rGO), resulting in the flaky structure.  The as-fabricated CoS2 based rGO composite exhibits improved sodium storage capacity compared with bare CoS2 as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  After cycling for 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1, the CoS2 based rGO electrode still delivered a reversible capacity of 192 mA h g-1.  The enhanced electrochem. performances of the CoS2 based rGO composite can be ascribed to the formation of a robust, conductive and high surface area composite.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoF-vIZETvkLLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li7nUdgQc4GNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1Slur%252FJ&amp;md5=ee4103cc8f9f5c91d2796250e648894d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-016-0981-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Synthesis and Electrochemical Sodium Storage of CoS<sub>2</sub> Micro/Nano-Structures</span>. <i>Nano Res.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">198</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">206</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis and electrochemical sodium storage of CoS2 micro/nano-structures</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xue; Zhang, Kai; Lei, Kaixiang; Li, Fujun; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer GmbH</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the synthesis and electrochem. sodium storage of cobalt disulfide (CoS2) with various micro/nano-structures.  CoS2 with microscale sizes are either assembled by nanoparticles (P-CoS2) via a facile solvothermal route or nanooctahedrons constructed solid (O-CoS2) and hollow microstructures (H-CoS2) fabricated by hydrothermal methods.  Among three morphologies, H-CoS2 exhibits the largest discharge capacities and best rate performance as anode of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Furthermore, H-CoS2 delivers a capacity of 690 mA·h·g-1 at 1 A·g-1 after 100 cycles in a potential range of 0.1-3.0 V, and ∼240 mA·h·g-1 over 800 cycles in the potential window of 1.0-3.0 V.  This cycling difference mainly lies in the two discharge plateaus obsd. in 0.1-3.0 V and one discharge plateau in 1.0-3.0 V.  To interpret the reactions, X-ray diffraction (XRD) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) are applied.  The results show that at the first plateau around 1.4 V, the insertion reaction (CoS2 + xNa+ + xe- → NaxCoS2) occurs; while at the second plateau around 0.6 V, the conversion reaction (NaxCoS2 + (4 - x) Na+ + (4 - x)e- → Co + 2Na2S) takes place.  This provides insights for electrochem. sodium storage of CoS2 as the anode of SIBs.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">CoS2 Nanoparticles Wrapping on Flexible Freestanding Multichannel Carbon Nanofibers with High Performance for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Yuelei; Cheng, Xudong; Huang, Yajun; Gong, Lunlun; Zhang, Heping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploration for stable and high-powered electrode materials is significant due to the growing demand for energy storage and also challengeable to the development and application of Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Among all promising electrode materials for NIBs, transition-mental sulfides have been identified as potential candidates owing to their distinct physics-chem. characteristics.  In this work, CoS2 nanomaterials anchored into multichannel carbon nanofibers (MCNFs), synthesized via a facile solvothermal method with a sulfidation process, are studied as flexible free-standing electrode materials for NIBs.  CoS2 nanoparticles uniformly distributed in the vertical and horizontal multichannel networks.  Such nanoarchitecture can not only support space for vol. expansion of CoS2 during discharge/charge process, but also facilitate ion/electron transport along the interfaces.  In particular, the CoS2@MCNF electrode delivers an impressively high specific capacity (537.5 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), extraordinarily long-term cycling stability (315.7 mAh g-1 at at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles), and excellent rate capacity (537.5 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and 201.9 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1) for sodium storage.  Free-standing CoS2@MCNF composites with mech. flexibility provide a promising electrode material for high-powered NIBs and flexible cells.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsuDlBVpRg67Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li7nUdgQc4GNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsFyrurbE&amp;md5=c481fd52012b54cae7f1e150c5213ca4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.12.018"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vogt, B.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultra-long cycle life, low-cost room temperature sodium-sulfur batteries enabled by highly doped (N,S) nanoporous carbons</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qiang, Zhe; Chen, Yu-Ming; Xia, Yanfeng; Liang, Wenfeng; Zhu, Yu; Vogt, Bryan D.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Efficiency, cost, and lifetime are the primary challenges for stationary energy storage with vanadium-redox flow and sodium-sulfur batteries as promising options.  In particular, room temp. sodium-sulfur battery systems offer the potential for safe, simple, low-cost and high energy d. storage, but the high reactivity or soly. of sodium polysulfides in common liq. electrolytes for carbonates or glycols, resp., leads to rapid performance loss on cycling.  Herein, we demonstrate a robust route to inhibit reactivity of the sulfides with carbonate electrolytes (and also inhibit the diffusion of polysulfides dissolved in TEGDME) and prevent performance loss on cycling using highly doped (≈40 atom%) nanoporous carbon from low-cost raw materials infused with sulfur as the cathode.  This cathode design leads to an ultra-stable room temp. sodium-sulfur battery with less than 3% decay in the discharge capacity after 8000 cycles at a high c.d. of 4.6 A/g.  At 0.23 A/g, the discharge capacity is approx. 400 mAh/g and stable over 350 cycles.  This combination of low cost and excellent cycle stability is promising for stationary, grid-level energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9Z5XxoMz15rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li7nUdgQc4GNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitFGisL%252FK&amp;md5=71736b09f059f5276abc6ff081398a1f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201800068"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Highly Reversible Na Storage in Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> by Optimizing Nanostructure and Rational Surface Engineering</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Self-Standing and Flexible Electrode of Yolk-Shell CoS2 Spheres Encapsulated with Nitrogen-Doped Graphene for High-Performance Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qiu, Wenda; Jiao, Jiqing; Xia, Jian; Zhong, Haimin; Chen, Liuping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Flexible lithium-ion batteries have recently attracted increasing attention with the fast development of bendable electronic systems.  Herein, a facile and template-free solvothermal method is presented for the fabrication of hybrid yolk-shell CoS2 and nitrogen-doped graphene sheets.  The yolk-shell architecture of CoS2 encapsulated with nitrogen-doped graphene coating is designed for the dual protection of CoS2 to address the structural and interfacial stability concerns facing the CoS2 anode.  The as-prepd. composite can be assembled into a film, which can be used as a binder-free and flexible electrode for lithium-ion batteries that does not require any carbon black conducting additives or current collectors.  When evaluating lithium-storage properties, such a flexible electrode exhibits a high specific capacity of 992 mA-h/g in the first reversible discharge capacity at a current rate of 100 mA/g and high reversible capacity of 882 mA-h/g after 150 cycles with excellent capacity retention of 89.91%.  Furthermore, a reversible capacity as high as 655 mA-h/g is still achieved after 50 cycles even at a high rate of 5C due to the yolk-shell structure and nitrogen-doped graphene coating, which not only provide short Li-ion and electron pathways, but also accommodate large vol. variation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQtMfBc3VH-LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKvO3qkKgYaQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjsFGhtb0%253D&amp;md5=6904a8363f5b2c976b1d39f72cbb9768</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1088/0953-8984/26/39/396001"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lyapin, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Utyuzh, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Petrova, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Novikov, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lograsso, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stishov, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Raman Studies of Nearly Half-Metallic Ferromagnetic CoS<sub>2</sub></span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Raman studies of nearly half-metallic ferromagnetic CoS2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lyapin, S. G.; Utyuzh, A. N.; Petrova, A. E.; Novikov, A. P.; Lograsso, T. A.; Stishov, S. M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physics: Condensed Matter</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">39</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">396001/1-396001/7, 7 pp.</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">IOP Publishing Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors measured the Raman spectra of ferromagnetic, nearly half-metallic, CoS2 over a broad temp. range.  All 5 Raman active modes Ag, Eg, Tg(1), Tg(2) and Tg(3) were obsd.  The magnetic ordering is indicated by a change of the temp. dependences of the frequency and the line width of Ag and Tg(2) modes at the Curie point.  The temp. dependence of the frequencies and line widths of the Ag, Eg, Tg(1), Tg(2) modes in the paramagnetic phase can be described in the framework of the Klemens approach.  Hardening of the Tg(2), Tg(1) and Ag modes on cooling can be unambiguously seen in the ferromagnetic phase.  The line widths of Tg(2) and Ag modes behave in a natural way at low exciting laser powers (they decrease with decreasing temp.) in the ferromagnetic phase.  At high exciting laser powers the corresponding line widths increase as temp. decreases below the Curie temp.  Then, as are shown, the line width of the Ag mode reaches a max. at ∼80 K.  Tentative explanations of some of the obsd. effects are given, taking into account the nearly half-metallic nature of CoS2.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrL14oLM9KYi7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKvO3qkKgYaQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhs1Omtb3I&amp;md5=e9ebab5755d01746aed61dfe01ca1265</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201608489"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, Y.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nickel sulfide nanospheres anchored on reduced graphene oxide in situ doped with sulfur as a high performance anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tao, Hongwei; Zhou, Min; Wang, Kangli; Cheng, Shijie; Jiang, Kai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">NiSx-rGOS is prepd. via a facile and cost effective hydrothermal process, with the structure of ultrafine NiSx nanospheres uniformly wrapped in the in situ S-doped rGO matrix.  The uniform nanostructural NiSx and high cond. of S-doped rGO (rGOS) can effectively increase the ionic and electronic cond. of the NiSx-rGOS composite, thus resulting in high capacity utilization of the active materials.  Moreover, the buffering layer provided by the rGOS matrix can accommodate the vol. change of the NiSx and protect the nanoparticles from aggregation during the repeated cycling process.  The as-prepd. NiSx-rGOS composite demonstrates a high reversible capacity of 516 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 with a capacity retention of 96.8% over 100 cycles and a remarkable rate performance of 414 mA h g-1 at 4 A g-1, possibly exhibiting the best electrochem. performances of nickel sulfide for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqKhgQ88vcmYLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljKvO3qkKgYaQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXmtVSjsLY%253D&amp;md5=5cfd5d40fb990bdcfc6d0773c9fa2aa8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1021/nn2006249"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, H.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Doped Graphene Sheets as Anode Materials with Superhigh Rate and Large Capacity for Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5463</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5471</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nn2006249</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2011%26pages%3D5463-5471%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DZ.-S.%2BWu%26author%3DW.%2BRen%26author%3DL.%2BXu%26author%3DF.%2BLi%26author%3DH.-M.%2BCheng%26title%3DDoped%2BGraphene%2BSheets%2Bas%2BAnode%2BMaterials%2Bwith%2BSuperhigh%2BRate%2Band%2BLarge%2BCapacity%2Bfor%2BLithium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fnn2006249&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b11984&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fnn2006249&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Doped Graphene Sheets As Anode Materials with Superhigh Rate and Large Capacity for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Zhong-Shuai; Ren, Wencai; Xu, Li; Li, Feng; Cheng, Hui-Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5463-5471</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A challenge in the development of Li ion batteries is to simultaneously achieve high power and large energy capacity at fast charge and discharge rates for several minutes to seconds.  N- or B-doped graphene can be used as a promising anode for high-power and high-energy Li ion batteries under high-rate charge and discharge conditions.  The doped graphene shows a high reversible capacity of &gt;1040 mA-h/g at a low rate of 50 mA/g.  More importantly, it can be quickly charged and discharged in a short time of 1 h to several tens of seconds together with high-rate capability and excellent long-term cyclability.  For example, a high capacity of ∼199 and 235 mA-h/g was obtained for the N-doped graphene and B-doped graphene at 25 A/g (∼30 s to full charge).  Probably the unique 2-dimensional structure, disordered surface morphol., heteroat. defects, better electrode/electrolyte wettability, increased inter-sheet distance, improved elec. cond., and thermal stability of the doped graphene are beneficial to rapid surface Li+ absorption and ultrafast Li+ diffusion and electron transport.  The doped materials are accordingly superior to pristine chem. derived graphene and other carbonaceous materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrG32RrUOW2FLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgulKZP11CuKQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXotFSnurY%253D&amp;md5=268fbeed11570fb540ed3dcf9fec79cb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201607469"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, G.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Mech. and chem. degrdns. of high-capacity anodes, resulting from lithiation-induced stress accumulation, vol. expansion and pulverization, and unstable solid-electrolyte interface formation, represent major mechanisms of capacity fading, limiting the lifetime of electrodes for lithium-ion batteries.  Here we report that the mech. degrdn. on cycling can be deliberately controlled to finely tune mesoporous structure of the metal oxide sphere and optimize stable solid-electrolyte interface by high-rate lithiation-induced reactivation.  The reactivated Co3O4 hollow sphere exhibits a reversible capacity above its theor. value (924 mAh g-1 at 1.12 C), enhanced rate performance and a cycling stability without capacity fading after 7,000 cycles at a high rate of 5.62 C.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A new direction for the performance improvement of rechargeable lithium/sulfur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Sheng S.; Read, Jeffrey A.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work we introduce a new direction for the performance improvement of rechargeable lithium/sulfur batteries by employing an electrolyte that promotes Li anode passivation in lithium polysulfide solns.  To examine our concept, we assemble and characterize Li/Li2S9 liq. cells by using a porous carbon electrode as the current collector and a 0.25 m Li2S9 soln. as the catholyte.  Results show that Li/Li2S9 liq. cells are superior to conventional Li/S cells in specific capacity and capacity retention.  We also find that use of LiNO3 as a co-salt in the Li2S9 catholyte significantly increases the cell's Coulombic efficiency.  More importantly, the cells with LiNO3 have a ∼2.5 V voltage plateau before the end of charging and demonstrate a steep voltage rise at the end of charging.  The former is indicative of the formation of elemental sulfur from sol. lithium polysulfides on the carbon electrode, and the latter provides a distinct signal for full charging.  Electrochem. analyses on Li plating and stripping in Li2S9 catholyte solns. indicate that LiNO3 participates in the formation of a highly protective passivation film on the Li metal surface, which effectively prevents the Li anode from chem. reaction with polysulfide anions in the electrolyte and meanwhile prevents polysulfide anions from electrochem. redn. on the Li surface.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo67P2PNhEjd7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgulKZP11CuKQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhsFWrurrE&amp;md5=8f433b9e515b3edd92e140ebc0a4c799</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1021/cm902050j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dudney, N.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchically Structured Sulfur/Carbon Nanocomposite Material for High-Energy Lithium Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Chengdu; Dudney, Nancy J.; Howe, Jane Y.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">This hierarchically-structured S/C nanocomposite material was tested as a high surface-area cathode for rechargeable Li batteries.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ formation of ultrafine CoS2 nanoparticles uniformly encapsulated in N/S-doped carbon polyhedron for advanced sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Fei; Lv, Tiezheng; Sun, Bing; Tang, Wen; Zhang, Chengzhi; Li, Xuanke</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">49</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A dragon fruit-like nanostructure consisting of CoS2 nanoparticles and co-doped carbon polyhedron is effectively prepd. through adjusting the pyrolysis processes of a Co-based zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF-67) precursor and subsequent heating sulfidation treatment.  It was revealed that ultrafine CoS2 nanoparticles with an av. particle size of 8 nm are uniformly dispersed and completely encapsulated in the N/S-doped carbon matrix.  Such a multifunctional architecture achieves the integration of the favorite traits of ultrafine active nanoparticles and heteroatom-doped carbon matrix, thus giving rise to much improved electron transfer and ion transport, and upholding the structural integrity of the electrode and electrode/electrolyte interface.  As an anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), the as-prepd. CoS2/C polyhedron electrodes exhibit high reversible capacity and good cycling stability.  For example, a reversible specific capacity of 563 mA h g-1 and a capacity retention rate of 90% with a remaining capacity of 510 mA h g-1 are obtained after 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1.  In addn., a superior fast charge-discharge capability is also demonstrated with reversible specific capacities of 307 and 288 mA h g-1 at large current densities of 1500 and 2000 mA g-1, resp.  These impressive results indicate that the ZIF-derived synthetic strategy is highly adaptable to design dragon fruit-like nanostructure consisting of metal compds./carbon nanomaterials with potential applications in high performance electrochem. energy storage devices and other environmental technol. fields.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo7M8fmUtsxlLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljGnvHryVH7xg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXpvFyju70%253D&amp;md5=63cc25f9a1fe9dd9f22bd8f3f55e5ecd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51');
